# Investigation: DRA AllocationMode API Change Impact Analysis

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes
**Task Type:** Impact Analysis (investigation only — no code changes)

## Scenario

The Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) scheduler plugin is being modified to allow `AllocationMode: All` from multi-node resource pools. Previously, this allocation mode was restricted to single-node pools only. Before this change ships, the team needs a comprehensive impact analysis.

## Your Task

Produce an impact analysis report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. All source files that reference `AllocationMode` or the DRA allocation logic
2. Which controllers and schedulers are affected
3. What test files cover the current allocation behavior
4. What performance implications exist (scheduler hot paths affected)
5. Which downstream consumers (kubelet, device plugins) would see changed behavior
6. Risk assessment: what could break if this change has bugs

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Scope of the change — what components are affected and why>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted, categorized by risk level>

## Recommendation
<Risk mitigation strategy and testing plan>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on tracing `AllocationMode` through the DRA plugin, scheduler framework, and kubelet

### Key Findings:

**Core Impact Areas:**
1. **Allocator Logic** - Three allocator implementations (stable, incubating, experimental) in `staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/` must handle device collections spanning multiple nodes
2. **Scheduler Plugin** - The DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase must validate multi-node allocations, with potential performance implications near filter timeout thresholds
3. **API Validation** - Current validation accepts "All" mode but doesn't explicitly enforce single-node pools; validation is implicit in the allocator
4. **Kubelet/Device Plugins** - Must handle allocations where devices come from different nodes than pod placement

**Risk Levels:**
- **HIGH**: Allocator core logic (validateDeviceRequest, allocateOne functions)
- **MEDIUM**: Scheduler integration, validation logic, device plugin communication
- **LOW**: Metrics and status management

**Critical Test Case Found:**
The codebase already contains a test case `"allocation-mode-all-with-multi-host-resource-pool"` showing the expected behavior with devices distributed across two nodes in the same pool.

**Recommended Safeguards:**
1. Run complete allocator test suite
2. Add E2E tests with real device plugins
3. Consider a feature gate for staged rollout
4. Monitor scheduler filter performance
5. Update device plugin developer documentation

The report includes specific code references, line numbers, and a detailed pre-release checklist

[]*resourceapi.ResourceSlice\\n64: \\tcelCache         *cel.Cache\\n65: \\t// availableCounters contains the available counters for each\\n66: \\t// resource pool. It acts as a cache that is updated the first time\\n67: \\t// the available counters are needed for each pool. The information\\n68: \\t// about each pool is never updated once set the first time.\\n69: \\t// This is computed bsed on information on the Allocator, so it will\\n70: \\t// be correct even for multiple usages of the Allocator.\\n71: \\t// The keys in the map are resource pool names.\\n72: \\t// The allocator might be accessed by different goroutines, so\\n73: \\t// access to this map must be synchronized.\\n74: \\tavailableCounters map[draapi.UniqueString]counterSets\\n75: \\tmutex             sync.RWMutex\\n76: \\t// numAllocateOneInvocations counts the number of times the allocateOne\\n77: \\t// function is called for the allocator. make(map[matchKey]bool),\\n118: \\t\\tconstraints:          make([][]constraint, len(claims)),\\n119: \\t\\tconsumedCounters:     make(map[draapi.UniqueString]counterSets),\\n120: \\t\\trequestData:          make(map[requestIndices]requestData),\\n121: \\t\\tresult:               make([]internalAllocationResult, len(claims)),\\n122: \\t}\\n123: \\talloc.logger.V(5).Info(\\\"Starting allocation\\\", \\\"numClaims\\\", len(alloc.claimsToAllocate), \\\"numSlices\\\", len(alloc.slices))\\n124: \\tdefer func() {\\n125: \\t\\talloc.logger.V(5).Info(\\\"Done with allocation\\\", \\\"success\\\", len(finalResult) == len(alloc.claimsToAllocate), \\\"err\\\", finalErr)\\n126: \\t}()\\n127: \\n128: \\t// First determine all eligible pools.\\n129: \\tpools, err := GatherPools(ctx, alloc.slices, node, a.features)\\n130: \\tif err != nil {\\n131: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"gather pool information: %w\\\", err)\\n132: \\t}\\n133: \\talloc.pools = pools\\n134: \\talloc.logger.V(5).Info(\\\"Gathered pool information\\\", \\\"pools\\\", logPools(alloc.logger, pools))\\n135: \\n136: \\t// We allocate one claim after the other and for each claim, all of\\n137: \\t// its requests. For each individual device we pick one possible\\n138: \\t// candidate after the other, checking constraints as we go.\\n139: \\t// Each chosen candidate is marked as \\\"in use\\\" and the process\\n140: \\t// continues, recursively. Retrying the claim under\n787: \t\t\t// different circumstances may succeed if it uses\n788: \t\t\t// subrequests and changing the allocation of some\n789: \t\t\t// prior claim enables allocating a subrequest here\n790: \t\t\t// which needs fewer devices.\n791: \t\t\treturn false, nil\n792: \t\t}\n793: \t\treturn success, err\n794: \t}\n795: \n796: \t// r.subRequestIndex is zero unless the for loop below is in the\n797: \t// recursion chain.\n798: \trequestKey := requestIndices{claimIndex: r.claimIndex, requestIndex: r.requestIndex, subRequestIndex: r.subRequestIndex}\n799: \trequestData := alloc.requestData[requestKey]\n800: \n801: \t// Subrequests are special: we only need to allocate one of them, then\n802: \t// we can move on to the next request. Input
{
  "content": "# Investigation Report: DRA AllocationMode API Change Impact Analysis\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Dynamic Resource Allocation scheduler is being modified to allow `AllocationMode: All` to allocate from multi-node resource pools, removing a current restriction that limits this mode to single-node pools only. This change impacts the allocator's validation logic, scheduler plugin behavior, and device pool semantics across multiple DRA subsystems.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nCurrently, the DRA allocator enforces that requests with `AllocationMode: All` can only work with resource pools that span a single node. The change removes this restriction, allowing a single pod to be bound to multiple nodes through a multi-node resource pool. This fundamentally alters:\n\n1. **Pool Semantics**: Resource pools (identified by `ResourcePool.Name`) previously implied single-node boundaries in practice. Multi-node pools with `AllocationMode: All` require allocations to be valid across node boundaries.\n\n2. **Scheduler Behavior**: The scheduler's Filter phase must validate that allocating \"all\" devices from a multi-node pool is compatible with pod placement constraints (node affinity, anti-affinity).\n\n3. **Node Binding**: Allocations that span multiple nodes need appropriate NodeSelector constraints to inform the kubelet and other components about valid device availability.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Core Allocator Validation Logic\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/stable/allocator_stable.go:408-485`\n\nThe `validateDeviceRequest()` function handles `AllocationMode: All`:\n\n```go\ncase resourceapi.DeviceAllocationModeAll:\n    // Lines 446-481: Validation for \"All\" devices\n    for _, pool := range pools {\n        if pool.IsIncomplete {\n            return requestData, fmt.Errorf(\"claim %s, request %s: asks for all devices, but resource pool %s is currently being updated\", ...)\n        }\n        if pool.IsInvalid {\n            return requestData, fmt.Errorf(\"claim %s, request %s: asks for all devices, but resource pool %s is currently invalid\", ...)\n        }\n\n        for _, slice := range pool.DeviceSlicesTargetingNode {\n            // Collects all selectable devices from the pool\n            for deviceIndex := range slice.Spec.Devices {\n                // Lines 465-476: Device selection and collection\n                selectable, err := alloc.isSelectable(requestKey, requestData, slice, deviceIndex)\n                if selectable {\n                    device := deviceWithID{...}\n                    requestData.allDevices = append(requestData.allDevices, device)\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    requestData.numDevices = len(requestData.allDevices)\n```\n\n**Current Behavior (Before Change)**:\n- Validation allows \"all\" devices to be collected across all pools\n- The pools being iterated may currently include only single-node pools\n- Multi-node pools are rejected or not supported\n\n**After Change**:\n- Multi-node pools will be included in the iteration\n- Devices from multiple nodes will be collected into `requestData.allDevices`\n- The allocator will attempt to satisfy the allocation with devices that may span different nodes\n\n### 2. Device Allocation Core Loop\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/stable/allocator_stable.go:858-915`\n\nThe `allocateOne()` function processes \"all\" mode allocations:\n\n```go\ndoAllDevices := request.allocationMode() == resourceapi.DeviceAllocationModeAll\n\nif doAllDevices && len(requestData.allDevices) == 0 {\n    alloc.logger.V(6).Info(\"Allocation for 'all' devices didn't succeed: no devices found\", ...)\n    return false, nil\n}\n\n// Lines 892-914: Allocate all devices sequentially\nif doAllDevices {\n    deviceWithID := requestData.allDevices[r.deviceIndex]\n    success, deallocate, err := alloc.allocateDevice(r, deviceWithID, true)\n    if !success {\n        return false, nil  // ALL devices must be available\n    }\n    done, err := alloc.allocateOne(deviceIndices{..., deviceIndex: r.deviceIndex + 1}, allocateSubRequest)\n    if err != nil || !done {\n        deallocate()\n        return false, err\n    }\n    return done, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Behavior**:\n- All devices in `requestData.allDevices` are treated as a single atomic unit\n- If ANY device fails to allocate, the entire request fails\n- Devices from multiple nodes in the slice collection will all be allocated or none at all\n- The `allocateDevice()` function includes constraint checking (line 896)\n\n### 3. Test Case Evidence\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/allocatortesting/allocator_testing.go:5503-5520`\n\nA test case named `\"allocation-mode-all-with-multi-host-resource-pool\"` exists that shows the expected behavior:\n\n```go\n\"allocation-mode-all-with-multi-host-resource-pool\": {\n    claimsToAllocate: objects(claimWithRequests(claim0, nil, resourceapi.DeviceRequest{\n        Name: req0,\n        Exactly: &resourceapi.ExactDeviceRequest{\n            AllocationMode:  resourceapi.DeviceAllocationModeAll,  // Key: Mode is \"All\"\n            DeviceClassName: classA,\n        },\n    })),\n    classes: objects(class(classA, driverA)),\n    slices: unwrapResourceSlices(\n        sliceWithDevices(slice1, node1, resourcePool(pool1, 2), driverA,    // Device on node1\n            device(device1, nil, nil),\n        ),\n        sliceWithDevices(slice2, node2, resourcePool(pool1, 2), driverA,    // Device on node2\n            device(device2, nil, nil),\n        ),\n    ),\n    node: node(node1, region1),  // Pod scheduled on node1\n```\n\n**Key Insight**: The test shows:\n- Same resource pool (`pool1`) with `resourceSliceCount: 2`\n- Devices distributed across two nodes (`node1` and `node2`)\n- Both devices should be allocated despite being on different nodes\n- Pod is scheduled on `node1` but gets access to devices on `node2`\n\n### 4. API Type Definitions\n**Files**:\n- `pkg/apis/resource/types.go:1085-1092`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1/types.go:1143-1150`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1beta1/types.go:1160-1167`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1beta2/types.go:1149-1156`\n\n```go\ntype DeviceAllocationMode string\n\nconst (\n    DeviceAllocationModeExactCount = DeviceAllocationMode(\"ExactCount\")\n    DeviceAllocationModeAll        = DeviceAllocationMode(\"All\")\n)\n```\n\nThese constants are defined consistently across all API versions.\n\n### 5. ResourcePool Structure\n**File**: `pkg/apis/resource/types.go:223-240`\n\n```go\ntype ResourcePool struct {\n    Name string  // Pool identifier\n    // ... other fields\n}\n```\n\nResource pools are identified by name but may span multiple nodes. The allocation mode restriction is enforced in the allocator, not in the API types.\n\n### 6. Scheduler Plugin Integration\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:696-702`\n\n```go\nif pl.fts.EnableDRASchedulerFilterTimeout && pl.filterTimeout > 0 {\n    c, cancel := context.WithTimeout(allocCtx, pl.filterTimeout)\n    defer cancel()\n    allocCtx = c\n}\n```\n\nThe scheduler invokes the allocator with timeout constraints. Multi-node allocations may take longer to validate constraint satisfaction.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### HIGH RISK - Direct API/Allocator Changes\n\n1. **`staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/stable/allocator_stable.go`**\n   - Lines 408-485: `validateDeviceRequest()` - Validates \"All\" mode requests\n   - Lines 858-915: `allocateOne()` - Executes device allocation logic\n   - Risk: Must handle device collections spanning multiple nodes correctly\n\n2. **`staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/incubating/allocator_incubating.go`**\n   - Parallel incubating allocator implementation\n   - Must be updated in sync with stable allocator\n\n3. **`staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/experimental/allocator_experimental.go`**\n   - Experimental allocator variant\n   - Must be updated in sync with stable allocator\n\n4. **`staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/allocatortesting/allocator_testing.go:5503+`**\n   - Test infrastructure supporting multi-node allocation tests\n   - Already contains the test case for this scenario\n\n### MEDIUM RISK - Scheduler Integration\n\n5. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`**\n   - Filter phase (lines 450-750): Validates allocation feasibility\n   - Lines 696-702: Timeout handling for allocator invocations\n   - Impact: Multi-node allocations increase allocation complexity, may trigger timeouts\n\n6. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/noderesources/resource_allocation.go`**\n   - Lines 301-346: DRA extended resource scoring\n   - `calculateDRAExtendedResourceAllocatableRequest()` and `calculateDRAResourceTotals()`\n   - Risk: Must account for multi-node device pool calculations\n\n### MEDIUM RISK - Validation/API\n\n7. **`pkg/apis/resource/validation/validation.go`**\n   - Lines 268-286: `validateDeviceAllocationMode()` - Static validation\n   - Lines 788-798: `validateResourcePool()` - Pool structure validation\n   - Current validation accepts \"All\" mode; no explicit single-node check here\n   - May need additional dynamic validation\n\n8. **API Type Definitions (Multiple Files)**\n   - `pkg/apis/resource/types.go:875-878, 1000-1003`\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1/types.go`\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1beta1/types.go`\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1beta2/types.go`\n   - Risk: Type definitions unchanged; validation logic changes required\n\n### MEDIUM RISK - Kubelet/Device Plugin Integration\n\n9. **`pkg/kubelet/metrics/metrics.go:1080-1084`**\n   - DRA metrics tracking\n   - `DRAResourceClaimsInUseDesc` metric\n   - Risk: May need multi-node aware metrics\n\n10. **`pkg/kubelet/device-manager/` (if exists)**\n    - This change impacts the allocator's validation logic, scheduler plugin behavior, and device pool semantics across multiple DRA subsystems.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nCurrently, the DRA allocator enforces that requests with `AllocationMode: All` can only work with resource pools that span a single node. The change removes this restriction, allowing a single pod to be bound to multiple nodes through a multi-node resource pool. This fundamentally alters:\n\n1. **Pool Semantics**: Resource pools (identified by `ResourcePool.Name`) previously implied single-node boundaries in practice. Multi-node pools with `AllocationMode: All` require allocations to be valid across node boundaries.\n\n2. **Scheduler Behavior**: The scheduler's Filter phase must validate that allocating \"all\" devices from a multi-node pool is compatible with pod placement constraints (node affinity, anti-affinity).\n\n3. **Node Binding**: Allocations that span multiple nodes need appropriate NodeSelector constraints to inform the kubelet and other components about valid device availability.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Core Allocator Validation Logic\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/stable/allocator_stable.go:408-485`\n\nThe `validateDeviceRequest()` function handles `AllocationMode: All`:\n\n```go\ncase resourceapi.DeviceAllocationModeAll:\n    // Lines 446-481: Validation for \"All\" devices\n    for _, pool := range pools {\n        if pool.IsIncomplete {\n            return requestData, fmt.Errorf(\"claim %s, request %s: asks for all devices, but resource pool %s is currently being updated\", ...)\n        }\n        if pool.IsInvalid {\n            return requestData, fmt.Errorf(\"claim %s, request %s: asks for all devices, but resource pool %s is currently invalid\", ...)\n        }\n\n        for _, slice := range pool.DeviceSlicesTargetingNode {\n            // Collects all selectable devices from the pool\n            for deviceIndex := range slice.Spec.Devices {\n                // Lines 465-476: Device selection and collection\n                selectable, err := alloc.isSelectable(requestKey, requestData, slice, deviceIndex)\n                if selectable {\n                    device := deviceWithID{...}\n                    requestData.allDevices = append(requestData.allDevices, device)\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    requestData.numDevices = len(requestData.allDevices)\n```\n\n**Current Behavior (Before Change)**:\n- Validation allows \"all\" devices to be collected across all pools\n- The pools being iterated may currently include only single-node pools\n- Multi-node pools are rejected or not supported\n\n**After Change**:\n- Multi-node pools will be included in the iteration\n- Devices from multiple nodes will be collected into `requestData.allDevices`\n- The allocator will attempt to satisfy the allocation with devices that may span different nodes\n\n### 2. Device Allocation Core Loop\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/stable/allocator_stable.go:858-915`\n\nThe `allocateOne()` function processes \"all\" mode allocations:\n\n```go\ndoAllDevices := request.allocationMode() == resourceapi.DeviceAllocationModeAll\n\nif doAllDevices && len(requestData.allDevices) == 0 {\n    alloc.logger.V(6).Info(\"Allocation for 'all' devices didn't succeed: no devices found\", ...)\n    return false, nil\n}\n\n// Lines 892-914: Allocate all devices sequentially\nif doAllDevices {\n    deviceWithID := requestData.allDevices[r.deviceIndex]\n    success, deallocate, err := alloc.allocateDevice(r, deviceWithID, true)\n    if !success {\n        return false, nil  // ALL devices must be available\n    }\n    done, err := alloc.allocateOne(deviceIndices{..., deviceIndex: r.deviceIndex + 1}, allocateSubRequest)\n    if err != nil || !done {\n        deallocate()\n        return false, err\n    }\n    return done, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Behavior**:\n- All devices in `requestData.allDevices` are treated as a single atomic unit\n- If ANY device fails to allocate, the entire request fails\n- Devices from multiple nodes in the slice collection will all be allocated or none at all\n- The `allocateDevice()` function includes constraint checking (line 896)\n\n### 3. # Investigation Report: DRA AllocationMode API Change Impact Analysis

## Summary

The Dynamic Resource Allocation scheduler is being modified to allow `AllocationMode: All` to allocate from multi-node resource pools, removing a current restriction that limits this mode to single-node pools only. This change impacts the allocator's validation logic, scheduler plugin behavior, and device pool semantics across multiple DRA subsystems.

## Root Cause

Currently, the DRA allocator enforces that requests with `AllocationMode: All` can only work with resource pools that span a single node. The change removes this restriction, allowing a single pod to be bound to multiple nodes through a multi-node resource pool. This fundamentally alters:

1. **Pool Semantics**: Resource pools (identified by `ResourcePool.Name`) previously implied single-node boundaries in practice. Multi-node pools with `AllocationMode: All` require allocations to be valid across node boundaries.

2. **Scheduler Behavior**: The scheduler's Filter phase must validate that allocating "all" devices from a multi-node pool is compatible with pod placement constraints (node affinity, anti-affinity).

3. **Node Binding**: Allocations that span multiple nodes need appropriate NodeSelector constraints to inform the kubelet and other components about valid device availability.

## Evidence

### 1. Core Allocator Validation Logic
**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/structured/internal/stable/allocator_stable.go:408-485`

The `validateDeviceRequest()` function handles `AllocationMode: All`:

```go

    // Lines 446-481: Validation for "All" devices
    for _, pool := range pools {
        if pool.IsIncomplete {
            return requestData, fmt.Errorf("cla
